Pudong Boat Collision

▲Two Passengers Drowned

The Yang Sanbao, a boat from Pudong, set sail from Shanghai the other day, loaded with flour, sugar, northern goods, foreign cloth, groceries, etc. from Tongyuan and other shops, and more than ten male and female passengers. Yesterday, as dawn approached, it was sailing near Lujia Cliff when suddenly a boat from Xinchang, fully loaded with fresh fish, sailed towards Shanghai with its oars, moving at incredible speed. The Yang boat was unable to avoid it and was violently hit. The boat was smashed, and the male and female passengers were awakened from their dreams, rushing to the deck and calling for help. The Xinchang boat, seeing that it had caused the accident, rescued the passengers into the boat. The passengers saw that the Yang boat was sinking and became panicked, jumping and falling into the water. Three passengers fell into the water. The Xinchang boat rescued one passenger, who was soaked. Two passengers were missing. The Yang boat is now aground on the beach, but the goods are all wet, resulting in heavy losses. The Xinchang boat has been detained to claim compensation for the losses. The Shanghai shops were informed and hired a boat in the afternoon to go to the scene of the accident to investigate and transfer the goods to another boat. The two passengers who drowned were a Mr. Lu, a partner in a shop in Datuan, and a worker from a sock factory in Pudong. A boat has been hired to salvage the bodies.

A Fire on Route Lafayette Kills Five

▲The Shop Owner's Wife Jumps from the Building and Is Injured

▲The Oldest and Youngest Sons Die Saving People

▲The Maid Sacrifices Herself for One Hundred Yuan

At 2:15 a.m. yesterday morning, a fire broke out suddenly at the Changfa Cigarette and Paper Shop at number 108 Lafayette Road in the French Concession, burning five people to death on the spot, which is the most tragic loss of life in a fire this year. The details are recorded below.

The Translator Who Opened the Cigarette and Paper Shop: Suzhou Native Ding Chu

Tang, 66 years old, previously worked at the Danish Consulate at No. 1 Lyban Road in the French Concession. He was very good at foreign languages and once worked as a translator. Later, due to his age and fatigue and the large number of his children, he rented a single-room shop at No. 108 Lafayette Road, west of the intersection of Galle Road, in the French Concession to open the Changfa Cigarette and Paper Shop in order to make a living. The family lived in the shop.

The Family Situation: Ding Lost His Wife in Middle Age

Hair, his wife died early. The widow Xu is also from Suzhou. Together, they had three sons and four daughters. The eldest son, Changgen, is 18 years old and graduated from the West District School. The second son, Gengfa, is 13 years old. The youngest son, Caifu, is only 8 years old. The eldest daughter, Cui'e, is 37 years old and married to Guo Ziqing, the owner of the Yu Da Pawnshop at No. 60 Zhaozhou Road, Lafayette Road, who is from Guangdong. The second daughter, Xiuzhen, is 27 years old and married to Zhou Kanglin, who works at the Huangjiaku Helan Hotel in Ningbo. The third daughter, A Duo, is 15 years old and not yet married.

The residents of each room were nearly full. Ding's second son-in-law, Zhou Kanglin, had a son named Gui Di, aged eight. Previously, he also had a daughter named A Mei, aged twelve. Zhou also lived with his father-in-law in the front building at number 108. The small room in the pavilion was rented to a Mr. Chen. Ding himself lived in the back building. Mrs. Xu, along with A Mei, her young son Cai Fu, and the old female servant Fu Wu (aged seventy), stayed in the pavilion on the third floor. The eldest son, Chang Gen, and his niece Gui Di stayed in the attic on the third floor.

Elementary School Apprentice Reports Fire at Chang Fa Tobacco Shop

The business was thriving and there was an annual surplus. Unexpectedly, at 2:15 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the shop. The fire was fierce. Shi A Gen, a young apprentice, was awakened from his sleep and shouted to wake up his family, who all ran away. Ding escaped with his second son first, followed by his second daughter who also fled with her child. Ding's wife, Mrs. Xu, upon hearing the news, grabbed six hundred dollars in paper money and jumped from the window, injuring herself in the fall. The money was scattered on the ground and picked up by others.

Escaped, Then Ran Back In - His Eldest Son Chang Gen

First escaped with his younger brother Cai Fu, then ran back in to rescue his niece Zhou Gui Di and sister A Mei, but was overcome by the flames and could not escape, resulting in the brother, sister, and niece perishing in the fire. Furthermore, the servant woman Fu Wu, after escaping, ran back in to grab her own silver dollars, and also met her demise. The fire instantly burst through the floorboards, and red flames shot out from the roof. The fire brigade rushed to put out the fire, which was extinguished after about an hour.

After Yesterday's Examination, the Firefighters

Retrieved five charred bodies, large and small, all with burnt heads and faces, making them unbearable to look at. Subsequently, the police station dispatched detectives to carry the bodies to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan branch. The criminal investigation section of the French police reported to Judge Zhu of the French court, who arrived at noon to examine the bodies. He took his seat in court, and the detective first reported the circumstances. Ding Zhitang, the head of the business, was paralyzed from shock and unable to move. His eldest daughter, Guo Ding, appeared on his behalf. After questioning by Judge Zhu, Fu Renfu, the son of the servant woman Fu Wu, arrived to claim the body for burial. It was then announced that Ding Changgen, Ding Caifu, Ding Amei, Zhou Guidi, and the servant woman Fu Wu had been examined and confirmed to have died from burns sustained in the fire while still alive. Ding Zhitang, representing the deceased, was permitted to prepare coffins for burial, and Fu Wu's son was permitted to bury his mother. It is said that the shop had fire insurance of two thousand three hundred taels. The loss of goods and furniture in the shop is estimated at around five or six thousand taels.

Ferry Overloaded, Capsizes, Drowning Five People

Bodies Not Yet Recovered

Authorities Should Pay Attention

At 8:45 PM the night before last, thirteen dockworkers hired a Wusong sampan operated by a Suzhou woman named Xie at the Shuntai Wharf in Hongkou to cross to Pudong. The boat was small and there were too many people, making the situation quite dangerous. When the boat reached near the Xiangsheng Iron Factory in Pudong, it encountered a slightly larger wave, and the boat was unable to support the weight and sank in an instant. All the passengers on the boat, including Xie, fell into the water. However, due to thick clothing, most of them floated on the surface of the river, shouting for help. At that time, a Fuxing Company's Kang small steamship happened to pass by, heard the cries, and immediately stopped to attempt a rescue. The ship rescued passengers Ren Shigen, Zhang Honglu, Huang Fuqing, Chen Rongfu, Gao Renhua, Li Chenghua, Gui Chenglin, Xi Youlin, and the boat woman Xie, a total of nine people. Five other passengers could not be saved in time and drowned. Their bodies sank without a trace. The small steamship took the rescued people to the water police station, where they dried their wet clothes and were instructed to go ashore and return home. However, Xie was still responsible and was sent to the local court by Chinese detective Wu Rongsheng for disposition yesterday. The names, ages, and addresses of the deceased are recorded below: (1) Qian Fugen, 26 years old, from Pudong, residing at the east end of the Pudong Cao'an head; (2) Liang Linbao, 32 years old, from Jiangbei, residing at No. 22, Pudong Huayuan Stone Bridge; (3) Tang Gen, 31 years old, from Pudong, residing at No. 7, west end of the Pudong Third District Police Station; (4) Sun Liugen, 26 years old, from Pudong, residing at No. 24, Pudong 93rd Lane; (5) Gao Fubao, 30 years old, from Jiangbei, residing at No. 7, Pudong Huayuan Stone Bridge. It is heard that none of the bodies were found yesterday.

Twelve Extortion Letters from One Person

Authenticated by Detective Mei Yu of the Police Station

All Written by Gu Wannian

Yu Qing Testifies in Court

The Court Must Summon Cheng Linsheng

The home of Cheng Linsheng, a wealthy Anhui merchant residing at No. 1550 Jing'an Temple Road, received eight threatening letters delivered by mail last month, attempting to extort 30,000 dollars. The case was discovered by Chinese detectives Jin Yangwu, Liu Ronggen, and Bao detective Wang Daofu of the Jing'an Temple Police Station, who arrested the suspects Gu Wannian, the apprentice chauffeur hired by the Cheng mansion, Zhang Changshan, the gatekeeper, Wang Rusong, the accountant, and Yang Zhenyuan, the bodyguard of Yu Qing of No. 161 Yu Garden Road, and sent them to the Special District Court. According to Gu Wannian's initial confession, the matter was a conspiracy between him and Zhang, Yang, and Wang to extort money. He then suddenly recanted and denied the charges, and the matter was adjourned to a later date to summon Cheng to court for verification.

Mei Yu Authenticates - Yesterday morning, Judge Ge Zhitan reopened the trial. According to police lawyer Wang Yaotang, during the adjournment of the case, it was discovered that the defendants had also written four threatening letters in January of this year, delivered to the home of Yu Qing at No. 116 Yu Garden Road, attempting to extort a large sum of money. All the threatening letters in the two cases were sent to Mr. Mei Yu for authentication by the police station. Now that Mei has arrived in court, he can prove it.

One Person's Handwriting - Subsequently, Mei Yu testified that he works at the Shanghai Municipal Police Department. All the threatening letters, a total of twelve, were carefully enlarged and examined by me. I have determined that they were written by one person, the first defendant Gu Wannian. Because Gu had written several slips of paper at the police station, his handwriting was identical to the handwriting in the fourth letter received by Cheng Linsheng. The places where they are the same have been marked with an "X" next to the words.

You Are Rich, I Am Poor - Detective Jin also complained that all twelve letters were stamped with the post office date. According to my investigation, they were all issued by the Jing'an Temple Road Post Office. The victim Yu Qing also complained that he has been in the money business. At the end of the eleventh lunar month of last year, he suddenly received a threatening letter, which stated: "You are rich, I am poor, lend me 200 dollars. Although you have bodyguards, doormen, and Russian drivers, you only have three pistols. We have five pistols. If you do not agree, you must be careful of your life," etc.

Involving Bodyguards - Subsequently, he received a second letter demanding 60,000 dollars, with three locations for contact. He ignored all of them and did not report to the police station. When he received the third and fourth letters, the wording became even more intense and included words threatening to kidnap him, so he reported to the police. The third defendant, Yang Zhenyuan, has been my bodyguard since 1927, with a monthly salary of 54 dollars. His character has been good on weekdays. I did not know about Yang's arrest beforehand. When I saw it in the newspaper, I learned the reason for the arrest. Yesterday, a police detective came and told me to come to court today, so I am here. However, I do not know any of the defendants except Yang, etc.

Summon Cheng Linsheng - The defendants hired lawyers Fan Gang and Chen Ying to appear in court on their behalf. When questioned, Gu Wannian confessed that he wrote the five letters to Cheng Linsheng and the four letters to Yu Qing. He also wrote the addresses on three letters to Cheng, and Wang Rusong wrote two of the letters, and the author of one letter remained unknown. The rest of his testimony was the same as his previous confession in court. When questioned, the remaining three defendants still denied the charges. After Judge Ge verified the confessions, he ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and summoned Cheng Linsheng to court for verification.

Zhen Dan University Student Li Shusheng Attempts Suicide by Drowning

Neither Due to Economic Hardship

Nor Due to Romantic Disappointment

Perhaps Due to Failing Exams

Or Due to Contracting Madness

At 6:25 PM the day before yesterday, a handsome young man in a suit boarded the Longmao Zhan ferry from the Bund outside the Public Concession's Fourth Avenue to cross to Pudong. Just as it arrived at the Pudong dock, before it had docked, the young man, taking advantage of people's inattentiveness, jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. He sank in an instant, then floated up again. The ferry's sailors managed to rescue him and sent him to Police Chief Guo stationed at the wharf, who transferred him to the Third District. District Chief Zhang Mingqin ordered the police to take off his wet clothes. He was wearing a yellow woolen short overcoat, a serge suit, a wool undershirt, and a white linen undershirt. In his pockets, he had a total of 95 dollars in notes from the Bank of Communications and the Zhongnan Bank, 6 silver dollars, a watch, 18 cents in small silver coins, 22 copper coins, an order form from the National Clothing Company, a voucher from the Phoenix Men and Women's Hair Salon, a leather bag, and two complimentary tickets to the New World Company's rooftop garden. The young man's face was gray and he was shivering uncontrollably. He was ordered to change into an old police uniform. When asked his name, he refused to tell the truth. Late at night, he became slightly clearer and said his name was Li Shusheng, 19 years old, from Neijiang, Sichuan, and he was a student at Zhen Dan University in this city, residing at No. 30 Yongyi Lane, Jiangwan. He also had a younger brother named Xican, who was also studying at Datong School in Shanghai. When asked about the reason for his suicide attempt, he again stared blankly and did not answer. The district chief instructed the police to keep a close watch on him and investigated the school. It turned out that Li had asked the guard at the gate for a rifle that morning, intending to kill himself, but was unsuccessful. He also took a kitchen knife to cut his own throat, but it was also taken away, so surveillance was increased to prevent accidents. In the afternoon, his cousin Xie Xumu and classmate Wan Shi Wu brought a letter of certification from Zhen Dan University to the district and asked to take Li away. According to Xie, Li had a total of six brothers and a wealthy family. He was usually of upright character. It is difficult to believe that he suffered from economic pressure or romantic disappointment. The reasons for the suicide attempt were likely one of two: (1) Li failed the school's major exam last year, leading to thoughts of ending his life; (2) Li's father had suffered from madness for 16 years, or he was affected by hereditary influence. The district chief then allowed the two men to take Li away.

Miao Liucheng Confesses to Kidnapping Liu Tongyun

Conspiring with Ji Taozi and Others

The Court Adjourns for Re-Trial

Chinese detectives Shao Jingfan, Wang Youshan, Xu Decheng, etc., of the Gordon Road Police Station apprehended a bandit named Miao Liucheng (also known as A'er) from Jiangbei at No. 774 Taopeng Road the morning before yesterday and brought him to the police station. It was discovered that Miao was involved in the case of the kidnapping of Liu Tongyun, the manager of the Fuji Paper Shop in Chun Geng Lane, Ai Duo Ya Road, on the evening of September 19th last year, in which the perpetrators held weapons and demanded a huge ransom. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the police station sent Miao Liucheng to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court yesterday morning. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the case, saying that the French Police had arrested a criminal named Ji Taozi (also known as Xiao Taozi) in the case of the kidnapping of Liu Tongyun. He was interrogated by the French Court and sentenced to five years of imprisonment, after which he will be sent to the Mainland authorities for trial. Liu Tongyun lives at No. 434 Pu Bo Road in the French Concession and opened the Fuji Paper Shop in Chun Geng Lane, Ai Duo Ya Road. He had previously received a threatening letter. At 3:00 PM that afternoon, Liu took his own car, driven by the chauffeur Yang Afu, to the World Bookstore. After finishing his business, he returned to the shop at 4:00 PM. The chauffeur was dozing in the car. At 8:15 PM, Liu wanted to go out again. Just as he was getting into the car, four kidnappers suddenly came, brandished pistols, and threatened to make a scene. They forced Liu into the car and sped away. How Liu escaped afterwards is unknown. Liu has not appeared in court today and requested an adjournment. The defendant Xi Kai of the defendant confessed that he and Ji Taozi and four others kidnapped Liu and hid him opposite the bathhouse on Minguo Road. I was also monitored by those people, so I guarded the hostage with A'san and others. After Judge Ge Zhitan verified the confession, he said that the incident occurred in the jurisdiction of the General Patrol, and according to the court's trial procedure, the case should be handed over by the General Patrol. However, the police lawyer said that there is no specific procedure for handing over the case. Now that this case has been solved by the Gordon Road Police Station, it may be necessary to jointly handle it with the Chief Inspector's Office in the future. Judge Ge then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and re-examined in a week.

Strictly Prevent Ancient Artifacts from Leaving the Country

It has been repeatedly ordered by the government to strictly investigate and prohibit ancient artifacts from being smuggled out of the country by customs, and the Ancient Artifacts Preservation Institute has been purchasing and preserving them on record. It is now known that the Shanghai Municipal Government approved the official letter from the Ancient Artifacts Preservation Institute and yesterday ordered the Municipal Public Security Bureau to issue a notice to all districts under its jurisdiction that if any residents are found to possess ancient artifacts, such as jade and books, they should be reported immediately to notify the Ancient Artifacts Preservation Institute to send personnel to purchase them at a prepared price and send them to the institute for preservation, in order to prevent them from flowing to foreign countries and to value national essence, etc. After receiving the order, Director Chen has notified all subordinates to investigate and handle the matter accordingly.

The head of the police station immediately ordered several detectives to go together. However, the suspects in the house had already fled after hearing the news, leaving only a large box of printed counterfeit currency behind. A Must-Read Book for Young Men and Women

The content includes Liu Linsheng, former director of the Chinese Department of Jinling Women's University, on the theoretical aspect of marriage guidance; Lawyer Qu Shao Yi on the legal aspect of marriage guidance; Liao Mao Ru, vice president of Guanghua University, on the educational aspect of marriage guidance; Tang Qing Zeng, professor of Daxia University, on the economic aspect of marriage guidance; Ai Wei, director of the Department of Educational Psychology of Central University, on the psychological aspect of marriage guidance; Song Guobin, chairman of the Shanghai Medical Association, on the physiological aspect of marriage guidance; and writer Xu Qing Yu on the aesthetic aspect of marriage guidance. Each article is based on reason and guides men and women to solve marriage problems, so as to obtain a satisfactory spouse. Pan Gongzhan, director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, wrote a long preface, explaining the true meaning of love and acting as a wake-up call for young men and women, and praising the book as a needle in a haystack for young people's marriages. The book is also beautifully printed, with the cover designed by the famous painter Fang Xuegu. The price is 70 cents per copy, with a special price of 56 cents. Postage is 2 cents for out-of-town orders, and 6 cents for registration. The Shanghai Diligent Bookstore is located at No. 39 Xinminqiu, Malan Road, Lafayette Road, French Concession, Shanghai. Doctor Mao Houtian Cures Dangerous Diseases

Mr. Mao Houtian from Yiwu has been working in the Shanghai Local Court for a long time. He has been studying medicine for 30 years and has profound insights into all aspects of male, female, large, and small pulse diagnosis, and is especially skilled in the field of measles and smallpox. There has been an endless stream of people seeking treatment, saving many lives. For example, the measles of the wife of Wang Zhennan, the chief prosecutor of the Higher Second Court, the diphtheria of Judge Ge Zhitan, the dysentery of the wife of Tong Shenglü, the typhoid fever of Clerk Zhong Shizuo, and the smallpox of the son of Wang Yuncheng in Qunyufang, are all major and dangerous diseases, all treated by Dr. Mao alone, who managed to quickly bring about recovery, and they were all grateful.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom

— Cai Shangen

▲ In first love, one rushes to live together. After marriage, one rushes to separate. "All have a beginning, but few an end." This is true in the modern age.

▲ When in school, one often envies those who work in society. But after entering society to seek work, one envies the former self in school.

▲ When one is pursuing an ideal, one feels happy about everything. But after realizing it, one realizes that it is nothing more than that, and even feels that it is of no interest.

▲ Every time I see a small fox kept by a wealthy and noble person, being held in the arms of its mistress and going out in a car with her, I think of the poor and lowly compatriots who are far below them.

▲ Generally, in schools in large commercial ports, the faculty and staff are often commercialized. In the capital where the government is located, they are often bureaucratized. This can be proven by observing the schools in Shanghai and the former Peiping and the current Nanjing.

▲ The past is already dissatisfied with the present, and the present will also be dissatisfied with the future. It is truly as the saying goes, "Later generations will view the present as the present views the past. They have already attacked their predecessors and replaced them. Later generations will also attack them and replace them." In this, it can also be said that "The way people view me is the way I view people."

▲ The so-called happiness and suffering in the world are actually only temporary. Once happiness has passed, one no longer feels the happiness. Once suffering has passed, one no longer feels the suffering. But it does not stop there. Often, extreme happiness breeds sorrow. Therefore, happiness is not worth cherishing. Moreover, if a person has not suffered first, he will not be able to see the joy of what he later obtains. Therefore, suffering is also indispensable.

Professor Lu's Bronze Utensil Hobby

— Wan Cheng

Professor Lu Xirong (Jin Hou), Ph.D., of Great China University and former Director of Education of Yunnan Province, is honest and simple. He has been teaching at Great China for many years and has never casually missed a class. Even in heavy wind and rain, he arrives on time. His patient and encouraging teaching has always been admired by students.

Professor Lu has a hobby for bronze. His residence is on Mendeland Road. All the daily utensils in his residence are mostly made of bronze. In particular, there are many bronze antique objects in his study, such as bronze vases, bronze pen holders, bronze bookshelves, and various bronze birds and animals, which are precious and lovely. In short, everything in his study is made of bronze. Professor Lu is from Yunnan Province, and Yunnan produces copper. Could it be that the professor's bronze hobby is also due to geography?

Anecdotes of Wu Guandai

— Chen Boying

Wu Guandai was a native of Liangxi and a famous modern painter. Unfortunately, he passed away last year, and everyone who heard of it regretted it. A visitor narrated his anecdotes, saying that his family was originally poor and humble, but later it flourished. Truly, he was "the son of a plowing ox" and "the sweet spring has no source," so there is no need to discuss family background. When he was young, he studied with a tutor. One day, the tutor went out, and three friends came to visit but did not meet him and left. When the tutor returned, everyone told him that guests had come to visit. The tutor asked for the guests' names. The guests did not say their names, and no one asked, so they could not answer. The tutor was annoyed. Then, Wu Guandai stepped forward and said, "Since the guests' names are unknown, I still remember their appearance. Now, I will draw them for the teacher." He dipped his brush in ink and finished the drawing in a short time. One of them was thin, with a gaunt face, a high nose, and a slight beard. Another was fat and short, with small eyes and full cheeks. The third was of medium build and wore sunglasses. He presented the drawings to the tutor. As soon as the tutor saw them, he exclaimed, "These are my old friends Lin Fuchang, Liu Qixiang, and Lü Qianzhi! Why have they come?" Then, he turned to Wu Guandai and said, "I truly did not know that you possessed this skill. I hope you will not abandon it." It can be seen that Wu Guandai was rich in artistic talent. From then on, Wu Guandai was determined to pursue painting. However, at that time, those who studied painting with a teacher were required to pay a fee of 200 taels of gold, 10 shi of rice, and two banquets, and to lodge in the teacher's home for a period of three years. Wu Guandai could not afford it, so he could not become a student. Moreover, the true works of ancient masters were mostly collected by wealthy families, locked away and kept secret, and only those who were close friends were allowed to see them. Therefore, Wu Guandai went to mounting shops every day to admire their brushwork. After a long time, the shopkeepers became annoyed and refused to let him in. A man named Ding, who lived next door to the shop and had served in the capital, heard about this and was angry, saying, "Paintings are looked at all day long; does it lose a single hair? How can lowly workers be so arrogant?" He summoned the shopkeepers and reprimanded them, agreeing to let Wu Guandai watch without objection. Wu Guandai's painting improved day by day, and his figures and ladies were excellent. Few could compete with him. At that time, a fellow villager named Zhang Shouyi, who specialized in landscape painting, knew Wu Guandai and guided him to view the Song and Yuan paintings collected by the Qin family. Qin's ancestor was the author of *Tongyin Lunhua* (Essays on Painting from the Paulownia Shade). Having seen a wide range of works, Wu Guandai's own works became even better. Then, Zhang taught Wu to paint landscapes, and Wu taught Zhang to paint figures. Zhang could not succeed in painting figures, but Wu succeeded in painting landscapes. In a few years, his fame surpassed Zhang Shouyi. However, connoisseurs believed that he was not as good as Zhang Shouyi. Some said that his late works were mostly done by his disciples, and Wu only made minor corrections. Wu once accompanied Lian Nanhuzhi to Beijing and stayed for a long time, so his name spread throughout the north and south.

A Record of Director Chen's Oath Ceremony

— Sun Choucheng

Shanghai Public Security Bureau Director Chen Xizeng held an oath ceremony at 10 AM on the 2nd of this month. He invited people from all walks of life to participate in advance, and many attended. Here is a record of what I saw and heard.

I went at half past ten. When I arrived at the entrance of the Public Security Bureau, I saw that the road was blocked by people standing and looking around. After being asked for an invitation card by the guard, I was led to the signing desk at the second entrance to sign my name. Several dozen armed patrol teams were standing in the courtyard, lined up in rows, in an orderly manner. In front of the auditorium, a large shed of five bays was specially built, with four large characters "Oath Ceremony" hanging in the middle. Beside it were four bamboo cloth banners with the words "Relieve the People's Suffering," "Protect the People's Interests," "Complete the Model Police District," and "Promote the Spirit of Fearlessness." Inside the shed, all the respectful officials of the city were standing in the middle, with hardly any space. On both sides, there were three long tables arranged in a river shape, covered with white tablecloths. On the tables were tea and snacks provided by the Atlantic Western Food Company, as well as several cans of Mei Lanfang cigarettes. The guests were seated on either side of the tables. At that time, Mayor Zhang was giving a speech. Because the distance was too far, I could only see him speaking and gesturing, but I could not hear the meaning of what he was saying. Soon, I saw Central Committee member Chu Minyi, wearing a black cloak, standing upright in the police officer team. The greeter did not pay attention at first. When the master of ceremonies called out loudly to invite Committee member Chu to give a speech, he was led to the stage and given a seat. More than ten people of the opposite sex, all wearing leather-collared coats, stood around him. Because they were humble and did not sit down, I found it very strange. I then asked Hong Lanxiang, who said that these people were all female detectives, who were subordinates rather than guests, and I suddenly understood. When Yu Suqiao asked the guests to speak, no one responded. Mayor Zhang pointed to Ye Huijun, and everyone applauded in agreement. Ye Huijun did not decline further because someone was supporting him, so he went to the stage. Because Ye's speech was both serious and humorous, I couldn't help but listen, so I pushed my way inside. Ye said that Director Chen was a revolutionary comrade. He heard that after taking office as the Director of the Public Security Bureau, he had worked extraordinarily hard. He not only stayed in the bureau but also secretly went to various districts in the late night to examine the diligence of his subordinates. This kind of director cannot be compared with those who only think about three meals a day and sleeping at night. He also compared the recent rampant thieves, where the Chinese concession was safer than the foreign concession, but there were still such cases, to ordinary typhoid fever and latent typhoid fever, and asked Director Chen to prevent problems before they happen and treat them as soon as possible. His speech was humorous and amusing, and those who heard it laughed. After the ceremony, the guests went to the stage to congratulate the director. There were many people and the hall was narrow, which caused Director Chen to be surrounded. They shook hands one by one, and it took about twenty minutes to finish. I took this opportunity to visit the auditorium and saw the souvenirs presented by various circles, all displayed on the three tables under the portrait of Sun Yat-sen. In the middle were two two-foot-high silver tripods. Other silver cups and shields surrounded them. The engraved characters were dazzling and beautiful. Under the rectangular silver shield sent by Yang Hu was a piece of white paper six inches wide and eight inches long. Looking closely, I realized that it was the oath that Director Chen took today. The text was very simple, the characters were upright, and it was sealed with a small seal, which was quite solemn. Then, we went to the courtyard to take photos. The guests sat in the front row, and the police officers stood around in the back. The photographer took four photos for the sake of solemnity. Then, the meeting adjourned. I returned and wrote this record.

Record of a Difficult Birth of Twins

— Qingqu

A few days ago, a man named Jiang from the countryside outside the South Gate of our county had a wife who was giving birth. The delivery was difficult. The midwives were not familiar with the operation, which caused the baby to be injured and die when it was born. The matter was very strange, so I write this record of it.

Initially, I heard that the woman felt unusually severe abdominal pain and was quite worried. She called the midwife to come, but after a long time, there was no movement. The whole family was frightened, fearing that something might happen. They did not wait for the melon to ripen and fall, and the disaster began. Now the mother is still in a critical period.

At that time, the baby came out first. The head was very large, like a baby over a year old, or even more. However, due to the injury, the eyebrows and eyes were moved to the top of the head, and there seemed to be no beard below. Those who saw it were shocked and at a loss. Unexpectedly, after a while, another one came out, which was tiny, no different from a fetal cat. They were twins, and both were female.

Old customs consider strange fetuses to be unlucky. The news spread far and wide, and neighbors came to visit and watch. They all thought it should be exposed, not hidden, so it was hung on a power pole. Later, the city's public education hall heard about it and ordered people to collect it and store it in a glass bottle, filled with alcohol, for research.

Those who do not know think that one baby's skull is too large, so they consider it a monkey, and say that its ears grow under its ribs. These are all rumors and different words. One fetus's body development was incomplete, resulting in unequal comparison. They hastily said that a human gave birth to a monkey and a cat, calling it a fetal demon. This is truly a case of being surprised by rare things.

Some say that when these two fetuses first fell down, their backs were connected by flesh and could not be separated. Later, they were cut open with a knife, so now in the bottle, there are bloodstains on each back, which are still vaguely visible. The small one's ears droop down on the edges, which is different from the usual state. This is what is different. So I especially recorded it.

My View on *Journey to the West*

— Zhu Shiseng

Plays are inherently fake, but the performers must act seriously. Otherwise, it is not enough to move the audience. Therefore, writing a play is not easy, and the performers cannot be sloppy. The current play *Journey to the West* is popular on various stages and can be called a *Journey to the West* craze. The important characters in the play, such as Tang Sanzang, are not comparable to ordinary monks. He is indeed morally noble. Secondly, Sun Wukong's skills are superb, and his actions will never be like those of today's vulgar monks. Even Zhu Bajie and Sha Seng, whose skills are not as good as Wukong's, will never violate Buddhist rules. Moreover, they are Tang Sanzang's disciples, wholeheartedly and diligently following their master on the journey to obtain the scriptures. Their aspirations are extraordinary. This can be seen here. However, there is still evidence to verify Tang Sanzang. In fact, Wukong, Bajie, and Sha Seng did not exist. Today, various stages want to perform them as interludes. They must be cautious about their actions. If they add the ugly behavior of modern people to them, they will inevitably lose their original appearance. Isn't that a pity? You must know that everything benefits from morality, and enjoyment can last long. Otherwise, even if it develops, I am afraid it will be difficult to last. Although there is freedom of action under the clear blue sky and white sun, the Three Principles of the People still want to preserve our inherent good Chinese morality. I hope that the owners of various stages and the giants of the theater industry will still start with morality in the theater. Business is not difficult to have the hope of development. The future will certainly be grand.

Interesting Anecdote of an Ape Addicted to Smoking

— Cangfu

Years ago, I was a guest in Shouchun. At that time, Wang Hanming's Thirteenth Army of the Zhilu Army was stationed in Shouchun. The army had two cavalry battalions, which were trained by an ape. When the ape mounted the horse, it would advance; when it dismounted, it would retreat. Whenever it was dispatched, the ape was always given weapons to lead the way. One day, it was heard that the Party Army Yue Xiangru occupied Zhengyang. Wang督队 set off. It was already midnight. Wang first ordered the旅长 Song Yong'an of his unit to lead two infantry regiments as the vanguard, and he led the cavalry to follow behind. Unexpectedly, the ape suddenly fell off the horse in the middle of the road. When the cavalry saw the ape dismount, they all ran back. Wang suspected that the enemy had been discovered and followed the cavalry back to Shouchun. Afterwards, it was learned that the ape had a smoking addiction, which was caused by the ape keeper being an opium addict. Whenever he lay on his bed and smoked, the ape would sit and watch for a long time, and eventually became addicted. Every time it set off, the ape keeper had to spray it with smoke first, and the ape would be full of energy. This time, due to the urgent order, it did not have time to spray the smoke, and the ape's addiction flared up, causing this loss. This is also an interesting anecdote.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (130)

— Linghua

In Burmese custom, when the morning rice is cooked, they first send their son or daughter to wear the best dishes and rice on their heads to offer to the nearby temple. Then the monks eat by themselves. However, their love of giving may not be economical. A friend visited them. A family of several people could not afford food and clothing. When asked why, they said that they had dozens of yuan several years ago, which they gave all away, and now they have come to this. However, they do not regret it. Because if people are poor, they can become monks. After becoming a monk, it is easy to get alms, and it is not difficult to become rich. Lao Tzu said, "The more he does for others, the more he has himself. The more he gives to others, the more he has himself." Is this what the Burmese are talking about?

There are Indian performers who bury a bamboo pole on the street, which can be three or four zhang long. One person holds the bottom of the pole, and a man wearing chicken feathers performs. He climbs the bamboo to the top and performs various stretching exercises. It is not strange. After a while, he goes down to the ground, puts several tile pots on his head, and climbs the pole again. He can make various poses at the top, which is very difficult. It is an old Indian custom to swallow knives and spit fire. Therefore, this is just a minor skill.

On the 9th, I bought a local lacquer box, which is similar to the lacquerware of our Fujian, but slightly inferior in color. It can also be played with. Before leaving, I wrote a couplet for Pengcheng, saying, "The Han people are glorious, and Yao and Shun are civilized." At 12 o'clock, my clan sent me to the ship back to Yangon in two cars. I still took the boat that came to Bassein last time. Second class is nine yuan, which is what the English call "first class." There is no shower, and it is at the stern of the ship. It is not as good as the third class in the open on the boat, which has wind. And the price is three times as much. Therefore, the price of second-class and third-class boats and cars here is three times as much. I still live in the cabin that I came to last time. It is very hot, and there is no one to greet me. The tea room cannot be called. Tolstoy once said, "Only third-class cars can be ridden." I believe it. However, Chinese tourists go to foreign countries and sometimes take second class for the sake of face. In fact, in various regions of Southeast Asia, taking second class is the most disadvantageous thing. Because the waiters here do not entertain, and the berths are narrow and confined to a small room. It is far不如 being in a public place, as long as there is a mat, you can arbitrarily occupy the land of a square zhang. Taking a second-class cabin in a Southeast Asian ship is foolish. I know it and step into it. What to do?

On the ship, the moon at night is bright as a picture, illuminating the river is very beautiful. Only small insects come in search of light, so I dare not turn on the electric light.

At dawn on the 10th, I arrived in Yangon. The Burmese on the same ship got up a quarter of an hour earlier, and it took them about half a point to wrap their headscarves in front of the mirror. Westerners are very disgusted with the constraints of collar and tie and are willing to promote Chinese clothes. I especially hate the inconvenience of the tie. Men in Western suits are far inferior to women in terms of freedom. Now, the Burmese's headscarves are also difficult to dress up like this. It can truly prove the convenience of Chinese clothes, which are superior to all countries. Convenience is civilization.

Returning to Yangon, I still live in the Anxi Guild Hall. The Double Tenth Festival was very lively that day. The students paraded in cars.

Gold Price Plummets

▲ Cash Export Ban Rumors

▲ Gold Price Plummets Dramatically: Yesterday, March 4th, Plunged to 3.7 Taels

The market suddenly turned weak. It started calm in the morning but plummeted sharply at noon. The price fell by more than twenty taels, a rapid change that was unpredictable. The bid-ask spread was only a little over one tael to three or four taels, but the daily difference was as high as twenty-five taels. Foreign exchange rates also weakened. There were more sellers than buyers in the market. In the early market, companies such as Qian Changxiang, Cheng Feng, Yongxin, and Heng had sales, while Zhifeng, Yongtong, Taichang, and arbitrageurs were buying. The overseas silver market was calm, but there were buyers in both India and the United States, causing the gold price to open low. Later, there was a slight rebound, hovering around 770 taels. Around noon, rumors spread about a ban on cash exports and internal disputes in Japan, causing public panic. Overall, exchange rates eased, and major players actively sold off, creating an unfavorable environment. The market price declined sharply, falling twenty taels, and the outlook was weak. It suddenly broke through fifty taels, but still rebounded by five taels. Companies like Bingxing and Hanheng were selling, while Zhifeng Yong and retail investors were buying. On Wednesday, there was no market for exchange rates, and the final gold price was only 48 or 49 taels. This morning, it was predicted that large-scale short selling would increase by a quarter.

▲ Afternoon Trading Plunge Gathers Momentum: The April gold market opened lower by 2.4 mace in the morning, at 770 taels and 5 candareens. Large-scale forward contracts fell slightly by one-sixteenth, while recent contracts and silver prices remained unchanged. However, private telegraphs showed a rise of one-sixteenth, causing market sentiment to weaken. The price then fell to 69.5 taels. Soon after, Fuyu and others bought in, and because the British gold market was stable, Shanghai Mitsui and others offered May contracts at 124,375. Some in the industry bought, causing the gold price to rebound by 3 taels, reaching 72 taels and 7 candareens. However, retail investors sold again, causing the price to fall by 2 taels. The initial announcement was unchanged, with the price at 70 taels and 5 candareens to 1 tael 3 or 4 candareens. Afterward, the market was flat, with fluctuations of only one or two taels. Trading was slow. At 9:50 AM, the price was 69.5 taels, and around 10:30 AM, it reached 71 taels 2 or 3 candareens. Flour Market Mediocre

Yesterday, the flour market opened with a flat and tired pattern for all months in both the morning and afternoon sessions. Although foreign wheat quotes improved by one or two jiao, they did not have a significant impact on the overall price. However, major manufacturers continued to sell off their large holdings of foreign wheat, causing the longer-dated months to remain weak. The price for standard spot goods in the near-term remained around 2 taels and 2.5 candareens, which was far from the standard, so the market remained stable. As a result, the current month improved by 0.005 compared to the previous day, April decreased slightly by 0.005, May increased significantly by 0.005, June decreased slightly by 0.005, and July/August decreased slightly by 0.0025.

Wheat Futures Trend from Flat to Weak

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in both the morning and afternoon sessions, each month's market showed an initial stabilization followed by a tired trend. Initially, foreign quotes improved slightly, and prices for each month were similar to the previous day. However, in the afternoon sessions, the flour market was flat, and Australian wheat was offered at around 4 taels and 2.5 candareens, still available for purchase. Manufacturers, however, were still asking for high prices and were unwilling to continue purchasing. Given this trend, if deals were indeed made later, the psychology of most traders would be severely impacted. As a result, the current month through June each fell by 0.02 compared to the previous day, July was unchanged, and August fell by 0.04.

Social News

International Fixed Calendar

— Lin

The international "fixed" calendar is a new calendar that has never existed before. Since its invention, it has undergone research and improvement by many experts and is recognized as a new calendar that is most suitable for people's lives. Those who study this new calendar hope that it can be implemented from 1934. The League of Nations is also paying close attention to this matter and is scheduled to convene representatives from various countries in mid-October this year to hold an international conference on the calendar to solve and improve the calendar problem.

The so-called international fixed calendar, its characteristic is in the word "fixed". This new calendar stipulates that there are thirteen months in a year, four weeks in each month, and the four Sundays in each month have fixed dates. June 29th of each year is called Closure Day, and December 29th at the end of the year is called Year-End Day. It is stipulated as an international rest day. These two days are always the day after Saturday, but are not called Sunday. A month has only twenty-eight days, and all twenty-ninth, thirtieth, and thirty-first days are cancelled. The method is to take away thirteen days from June and eighteen days from July in the current calendar, a total of twenty-eight days, so there is another month. Easter Sunday is scheduled for April 15th, so the Lenten holidays of various churches will also have a fixed date and become permanent.

The fixed calendar, as the name suggests, means fixed and unchangeable, so every month is neatly twenty-eight days, seven days a week, the first day Sunday, the second day Monday, the third day Tuesday, the fourth day Wednesday, the fifth day Thursday, the sixth day Friday, the seventh day Saturday, and the eighth day is Sunday again. From then on, the 1st, 8th, 15th, and 22nd will always be Sundays, Monday will always be the 2nd, 9th, 16th, and 23rd, Tuesday will be the 3rd, 10th, 17th, and 24th, Wednesday will be the 4th, 11th, 18th, and 25th, Thursday will be the 5th, 12th, 19th, and 26th, Friday will be the 6th, 13th, 20th, and 27th, and Saturday will be the 7th, 14th, 21st, and 28th, so every month is like February of this year | 1931, only June and December of each year add one day to become a leap day, but it is not counted within the seven days of the week.

Looking at the current calendar, a month is either thirty days or thirty-one days, and February has twenty-nine days or twenty-eight days, so a month has either five weeks or six weeks. Like May of this year, the 8th has six weeks, and the 3rd, 10th, 17th, and 24th of May are Sundays, and the 31st is also Sunday. In August, in addition to the 10th, 9th, 16th, and 23rd being Sundays, the 30th is also Sunday. In addition, January, March, April, June, July, September, October, November, and December have five weeks, and February has only four Sundays. As for the date of Easter, it is even more uneven. For example, 1931 was April 5th, 1932 was changed earlier to March 27th, and in 1933 it was changed later to April 16th. The other holidays are the same.

With the above-mentioned changes, the current solar calendar has three unerasable shortcomings: (1) the number of days in each month cannot be averaged; (2) the dates and weeks (Sundays) in a month often change and cannot be unified; (3) religious holidays such as Easter change every year. There are three ways to remedy these shortcomings: (1) average the number of days in each month; (2) the dates and days of the week in the month are fixed; (3) Easter is scheduled for April 15th. The first method is to move the 31st of August to the end of each year, making February the 29th, so that the half-year period is exceptionally average. The second method is that each quarter has three months, becoming thirty days, thirty days, and thirty-one days, or thirty-one days and thirty days. Its advantages are (1) half a year or a quarter has a sufficient number of months and weeks; (2) the days and cycles in each quarter repeat cyclically; (3) each month has the same number of working days; (4) the first year after the change does not require much sorting for comparison statistics, etc. The third method is the international fixed calendar mentioned here, with thirteen months a year and twenty-eight days a month, becoming four whole weeks. The convenience of this new calendar is described below in separate items:

(1) Each month is average and the same as twenty-eight days and four weeks, circulating back and forth, never losing

Page 16

The economic value of the average month; (2) The correspondence between Sunday and the date of the month is permanent and unchanged. All clocks and watches can be used permanently; (3) Paydays, market days, regular markets, and meetings cycle back and forth, with the same date in each month without any mistakes; (4) A month is four weeks, so each week is a quarter of a month, so the dates of weekly pay, rent, and account payments are neat and consistent, without any discrepancies; (5) Save time and economy, and avoid disputes caused by date confusion; (6) Each Sunday and the four fixed days in a month return and forth, determined and unchanged. Therefore, various matters such as weekly or monthly work, production, business, payment, collection, and social interaction are exceptionally neat in terms of date; (7) Bills and drafts will never be due on Sundays; (8) Holidays for the public, families, shops, schools, and institutions all have fixed and unchangeable dates; (9) Income and expenditure can be equal at any time, or several times each, and can be accurately calculated; (10) The end of each month coincides with the last day of the week and remains unchanged, which is of great convenience for business and rent, etc.; (11) Public, commercial, financial, and family life are greatly facilitated by the zero days at the end of the week and quarter; (12) The fifth week's rent and wages in any uneven month can be saved without payment, which can save costs and help progress, and statistics are easy to organize; (13) The number of days between any two dates can be calculated at a glance, which is very convenient for paying wages, interest, and calculations. For example, to find out how many days there are from January 10th to June 20th, just multiply 28 by 5, which equals 140 days, and then add 10 to get the answer of 150 days; (14) Because the distance of each month is average and the Sundays of each month are the same, when doing statistics for government agencies, import and export companies, science, health, municipal administration, and families, not only can accurate ups and downs indices be obtained, but also valuable time for making annotations or revisions can be saved, and senior personnel can obtain accurate business trends at the end of the month to determine the administrative policy for the next month.

The fixed calendar also has considerable convenience for the women's world: (15) A month of twenty-eight days is exactly four weeks, which is very natural, so women often use twenty-eight days to calculate the changes in their body, and humans are produced after two hundred and eighty days, and half of humans are women, if a calendar of twenty-eight days a month is used, they can get great benefits in terms of personal calculation, because there is an accurate date from one to ten months, and they are very convenient in managing housework and accounts every day, every month, and every week, and especially suitable for public, private, and family appointments. They do not need to use monthly expenses or salaries to purchase food and other items for the fifth week, as they do now; (16) It can save the country, businesses, and individuals time and money to find or mention the dates on the calendar to determine the appropriate dates for work, payment, communication, and meetings, etc. Sentences such as "the Tuesday after the first Monday" and "the second and fourth Fridays" commonly used in laws, rules, and regulations can be omitted, and a lot of printing and advertising costs can be saved. Even in the United States alone, this cost can save about $30,000,000 per year; (17) If a fixed calendar of thirteen months a year and twenty-eight days a month is used, then the current economic value of labor, salary, rent, subsidies, etc., which circulates twelve times a year, can circulate thirteen times a year, so for every thirty-one yuan of circulating capital, only twenty-eight yuan is enough to replace it, because it circulates thirteen times a year, and the number of twenty-eight yuan can do the work of the current thirty-one yuan. The payment for the fifth week of the month can be completely cancelled. According to estimates, if a fixed calendar of one month and twenty-eight days is adopted, the economic value used in commerce in Europe during the initial three-month period of implementation can be reduced by at least 2,000,000,000 yuan. If all countries are included, the number will reach 5,000,000,000 yuan, equivalent to 1,000,000,000 pounds sterling; (18) The average bad debts and outstanding debts per month can be permanently reduced by 10%, with a ratio of 31 yuan to 28 yuan; (19) It can save the cost of printing and distributing the annual calendar; (20) Birthdays and anniversaries have fixed dates; (21) Easter has a fixed date, and Christmas and New Year holidays are linked to weekend holidays; (22) It can help select the dates for "Daylight Saving Time"; (23) It can help farmers cultivate fields; (24) It can help scientific and health research work.

The fixed calendar of twenty-eight days a month mentioned above has a total of twenty-four advantages, among which (1), (4), (9), and (14) are particularly important. However, the end-of-year day, that is, the day after December 28th, must be added, otherwise the above-mentioned many advantages cannot be obtained. Regarding this point, it seems that there is an eighth day in addition to the seven days of a week, and Jews and Seventh-day Adventists may object, but 99% of the people in the world are willing to obtain the various benefits mentioned above.

Marshal Foch's European War Diary (Continued)

— Translated by Gu Angruo

Our conversation in Saint-Pol was naturally about the situation of the Allied forces and the defensive line we had established on the Aisne River. Now we want to extend that defensive line to the coast. I told him that I had decided to have the soldiers dig trenches to resist the enemy's superior military equipment, and then take the offensive again when we also had the same reliable equipment, because this is the only way to win. Later, Mr. Lloyd George repeatedly asked me to remember this conversation, which he named "the Saint-Pol Plan." He watched that plan succeed.

The most important battle in the European War occurred under these circumstances. The Allied forces still wanted to strike first, and wanted to use the freedom of action given to them by the victory of the Marne to preempt the enemy's offensive, and wanted to take advantage of the enemy's victory in Antwerp before they could transfer troops to join the strong reserve forces arriving from Germany to launch a strategic offensive in this only theater of war to resolve the war on the Western Front.

The question I had to ask myself was whether we had enough time to gather the scattered and complex three Allied forces into a sufficient number to properly organize and cooperate to contain the enemy's plan and achieve the victory we deserved. If we could not have this expectation, we should at least prevent the enemy from succeeding. The great battle of Flanders soon answered this question.

This battle included two phases:

(1) The offensive along the coast, or the Battle of the Yser (October 17th to November 1st);

(2) The Battle of Ypres, Ypres is the transportation center of the Flanders region (October 21st to November 12th);

The Battle of the Yser

The area around Dunkirk was completely devoid of high ground, trees, or anything to rely on, and there were no railways or rivers to guard. However, if we were to prevent excessive retreat and avoid endless disasters in the future, a decision should be made without delay. I mean to pay attention to the railway line between Nieuport and Diksmuide. This railway at least provides a connecting line. Soldiers retreating there must cross it and can be told to stop. So this is a convenient base for reorganizing the ranks.

A railway often passes through ditches or fortifications, and even sunken wood and gravel on the plain can be used as a barrier to avoid artillery fire. So I adopted this route as a small protection for the soldiers lined up behind it. Moreover, the two ends of the railway are firmly attached to Nieuport and Diksmuide, so it can become a very valuable defensive line.

This was my belief, but I exchanged opinions with the Belgian General Staff (which I did not fully understand) and, based on the results, decided to have the Belgian army retreat to the end of the route and deploy defenses behind the route. A brigade of the 42nd Division in the north guarded Nieuport, another brigade in the center defended to Pervijze, and Diksmuide was defended by the Marine Corps. (To be continued)
